  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d9203efb-6aec-4b80-a936-a52a8bc92f2d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

So when the spirit of a cat is killed, yes, they do disappear because their spirit and<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In StarClan, it is not a cat but more of the spirit of the cat. So when the spirit of a cat is killed, yes, they do disappear because their spirit and their body have both been slain.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17966181929521513642">I love this (these) series by Erin Hunter, I hope this isn't the last book though! <br/>I just wish it'd been a tad more clear about who Dovewing chooses, Tigerheart or Bumblestripe!<br/>I love that Cinderheart finally accepts Lionblaze, about time girl!<br/>I think Jayfeather is still my favorite character, he's just so grumpy and lovable at the same time, hehe. <br/>I wish Hollyleaf didn't die, I really did like her. She died saving Ivypool though, so it was a good death, a warriors death.<br/>I'm glad Star Clan helpe</span>
  <span id="freeText17966181929521513642" style="display:none">I love this (these) series by Erin Hunter, I hope this isn't the last book though! <br />I just wish it'd been a tad more clear about who Dovewing chooses, Tigerheart or Bumblestripe!<br />I love that Cinderheart finally accepts Lionblaze, about time girl!<br />I think Jayfeather is still my favorite character, he's just so grumpy and lovable at the same time, hehe. <br />I wish Hollyleaf didn't die, I really did like her. She died saving Ivypool though, so it was a good death, a warriors death.<br />I'm glad Star Clan helped out, and so did the Ancient cats, Midnight, and Rock. I don't understand anything about Rock really, except he's blind, really old, grumpy (more so than even Jayfeather), and hideous.<br />This <b> cannot </b> absolutely <b> cannot, </b> be the last installment of the Warriors!! I can't have memerised all those names and cats for it to end like this!!! <i> Noooooo..... </i> Please, keep writing! I've read every single novel (not all the manga regrettably) and loved them <i> all! </i> </span>

<div id="review_315992846" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315992846" />
    <a title="TeaDrinkingCat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4965293-teadrinkingcat"><img alt="TeaDrinkingCat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444189287p2/4965293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315992846?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TeaDrinkingCat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TeaDrinkingCat" href="/user/show/4965293-teadrinkingcat">TeaDrinkingCat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315992846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11170602404719384412">It all started in 2008, and I had just won the State Reflections contest. I never made it to nationals, but as a petty gift I got a ten dollar Borders gift card.<br/><br/>When I ran into get a book, I was late to my aunts house, and I had to pick anything, as quick as possible. I saw a light green novel, with an orange cat on the front.<br/>Now, I had always been a fan of felines, as I had one myself. I knew this book would be good, so I simply grabbed it and purchased it. I then left Borders.<br/><br/>This was in the b</span>
  <span id="freeText11170602404719384412" style="display:none">It all started in 2008, and I had just won the State Reflections contest. I never made it to nationals, but as a petty gift I got a ten dollar Borders gift card.<br /><br />When I ran into get a book, I was late to my aunts house, and I had to pick anything, as quick as possible. I saw a light green novel, with an orange cat on the front.<br />Now, I had always been a fan of felines, as I had one myself. I knew this book would be good, so I simply grabbed it and purchased it. I then left Borders.<br /><br />This was in the beginning of summer, and it took me all of that time to finish the book. It was good, granted, but for some reason it just didn't move me until the end. I found myself going to Borders and purchasing more and more of these unique novels, and finding myself slightly embarrassed to be seen with them. They were fairly short, even for a fifth grader, and the cats on the front didn't help.<br /><br />But I loved them. I loved them so, so much. I grew very close to the character Silverstream. And once I was googling fan art, and one of the websites a piece of work was on was..... Goodreads. It was in the group Firestar Fans. I joined the group after making an account, choosing my screen-name to be Silverstream. I kept that name for three years, until finally changing it to match my Deviantart account file. <br /><br />Many people would take a glance at these books and think they are odd, and aren't real literature. But they've sparked a huge chain reaction in my life, one that led to me discovering the Internet, getting new friends, and becoming and artist. <br /><br />And that if my first thanks. To that reflections contest. To that single Borders gift card. And to the Erins. Without them, I don't know how I would spend my life. This series will always have a place in my heart. <br /><br /><br />Now, time for the actual review.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />I always loved the concept of the Dark Forest, but it always bothered me how stupid the cats were for simply falling for this stupid trick. In this novel we found out why they did; they were held against their own lives. A cat who I shall not name was murdered in cold blood by Brokenstar after defying his choices. <br /><br />Dovewing and Tigerheart. I never liked Tigerheart, from the moment Tawnypelt named him after her father. He just seemed like he, too, would grow to inherit his grandfather's evilness, and, in a way, he did. <br />It was cute how he would meet up with Dovewing, but after awhile, it bothered me, especially when Bumblestripe got involved. I knew he was adorable and suited her, and Tigerheart would just add more stupid kits being born half-clan.<br /><br />Ivypool did a good job acting in the Dark Forest, I actually got to realize that she thinks. I hated her for awhile, mostly since she was jealous of her sister for awhile. But she did receive some respect, but I feel like it was necessary for her to die in the book. I think she should have sacrificed herself for her sister.<br /><br />Firestar. Oh, how I cried when he died. All the fans online say they hate him, but I just can't imagine hating him. Firepaw, who started the whole series, start to end, dying? I knew I would bawl. His death did seem very confusing for me, with the smoke billowing around him, and then he just died. He should have died protecting Sandstorm, or even Hollyleaf. Die protecting someone. Not by Tigerstar. <br />But his face off with him was fairly epic. I cried so hard when Bluestar recited all of his nine lives, as it was very emotional for me.<br /><br />Ferncloud. Almost the worst of all the deaths. I always felt Dustpelt was amazing paired up with her, and how she loved all the kits she had. She was always one of my favorites. I loved when her spirit rose, Amberkit mewed, "Ferncloud's awake!" I found myself crying very hard then. <br /><br />Spottedleaf. I never particularly liked this cat. Mostly because I feel she tried to take Firestar away from Sandstorm. But when she double-died, I felt myself crying for Firestar. His breakdown was amazingly executed, saying things like, "You said you would be waiting for me in StarClan!" etc. <br /><br />Unnamed kit. I believe it was in ShadowClan where a random kit died, its mother huddling over it. This was the first somewhat impacting death. I knew everything was about to get much more serious when I read about the dead kitten, and I knew this would slowly get amazing.<br /><br />Hollyleaf.<br />I absolutely hated her death. This was a no-no for me. Not much more to add; it was sad. I cried.<br /><br />And of course, Bramblestar appointing Squirrelflight deputy. This made me want to gag. I've always hated her from the start, I used to like Leafpool, but after what they did to their children and Brambleclaw, I've always been willing to let them die. Bramblestar making her deputy wanted to make me kill myself. Terrible. He should have appointed Cinderheart, after all, her path was to walk that of a warrior; what nobler way as a leader?<br /><br />That's it for now, I might add more later. Overall, a great novel, and I am somewhat willing to try the new Survivors Series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11170602404719384412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159697753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159697753" />
    <a title="Micheline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline"><img alt="Micheline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520260852p2/4845030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159697753?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Micheline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micheline" href="/user/show/4845030-micheline">Micheline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061555275" href="/book/show/12036852-the-last-hope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=creature-characters">creature-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4845030-micheline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159697753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15316209554819734623">The Last Hope is the final installement in the final series of Warriors books (chronilogically since 'the Erins' have said they would write a sort of prequel or origins series eventually). Words cannot describe how I have enjoyed this series as a whole. I got into it skeptically; wondering if even my love of cats wouldn't be enough to make a whole series of books with cat protagonists interesting. Thinking these were children's books that would probably bore me eventually...boy was I wrong. Thes</span>
  <span id="freeText15316209554819734623" style="display:none">The Last Hope is the final installement in the final series of Warriors books (chronilogically since 'the Erins' have said they would write a sort of prequel or origins series eventually). Words cannot describe how I have enjoyed this series as a whole. I got into it skeptically; wondering if even my love of cats wouldn't be enough to make a whole series of books with cat protagonists interesting. Thinking these were children's books that would probably bore me eventually...boy was I wrong. These books have more loss, grief, death and violence than most YA books out there, let alone children's books. There's something so utterly raw about these books; the emotions, the instincts. These cats are almost human...but much more primal. It's both simple and complex and it just tugs at the heartstrings. I think so many readers overlook this series because they think it odd or even childish as I once did and I'm so glad I took a chance on The Warriors...what a ride!<br /><br />But back to 'The Last Hope'. I think it's fair to say that the whole 'Omen of the Stars' series has been a set-up for this book. The Dark Forest is rising, kept 'alive' by mere memory, they are training tirelessly to eventually cross over to the living world and face the four clans in battle. Starclan is no longer of any help to the living, as they too fear the Dark Forest. It's up to the three of the prophecy; Jayfeather (♥), Lionblaze and Dovewing, to find the fourth cat prophesised. They must find the forth before light and dark meet in the final battle. I was a bit surprised to find that 'The Last Hope' got off to an almost slow start. I think it was mostly my expectations that the whole book would be one explossive installement. I would have docked maybe half a star if the ending hadn't made up for it. The Erins did indeed need to tie up some loose ends...set up some events up for the final battle looming. Once things start moving however: WOAH! The pacing is lightening speed and the shared narratives give the story even more intensity; kinda like the jerky camera movements action film-makers are so keen on these days, only without making you nauseous. :) As always battles in 'The Warriors' books are a gruesome affair. NO ONE is safe; the elderly and the young die in battle just like the rest of the Warriors.<br /><br />I really enjoyed how most loose ends from the previous series came into play. Past storylines for Firestar, Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight, Leafpool and many more re-emerged and were resolved. Fans of the previous series will be pleased. Personally in the past two series my favorite has always been Jayfeather, and he will join Brambleclaw (♥!!) and of course Firestar as all-time favorite characters; so I enjoyed the way everything ended and while we suspected this ending was coming <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ for Firestar ...ugh so sad! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> there were still some surprises along the way. I did find the last chapters were abrupt; everything happened so fast it was almost anticlimactic. But with me, theres always a longing when a beloved series ends...for it to go on. I deeply long to see my characters *after* all the ordeals; when they know peace and the war is over, I long to join them as they...go on. I can't wait to re-read the whole freaking series eventually. From 'Into the Wild' with no interruption till 'The Last Hope' with all the Super Edtions in chronological order, cause I'm a nerd like that! <br /><br />All in all it ones quite a memorable and emotional ride with The Warrior Cats and I'm couldn't be happier I took a chance on these books way back when!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15316209554819734623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_527263973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527263973" />
    <a title="Melissa Corn ~bubbles bubbles bubbles~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5197630-melissa-corn-bubbles-bubbles-bubbles"><img alt="Melissa Corn ~bubbles bubbles bubbles~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379896917p2/5197630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527263973?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Corn ~bubbles bubbles bubbles~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Corn ~bubbles bubbles bubbles~" href="/user/show/5197630-melissa-corn-bubbles-bubbles-bubbles">Melissa Corn ~bubbles bubbles bubbles~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527263973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13265510975251384421">I am writing this review in February which way after I actually read the book (which was in October or something I think) so a few of the things are a bit hazy to me. <br/><br/><br/> <b>Likes:</b><br/><br/>* I really enjoyed the fact that Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight and Leafpool FINALLY made up. I am so so glad that the drama with them is finally over.<br/><br/>* Hollyleaf's death scene: sure it was sad but in my humble opinion it was really well written and probably the best authored scene in the entire book.<br/><br/>* Bramblstar became leader </span>
  <span id="freeText13265510975251384421" style="display:none">I am writing this review in February which way after I actually read the book (which was in October or something I think) so a few of the things are a bit hazy to me. <br /><br /><br /> <b>Likes:</b><br /><br />* I really enjoyed the fact that Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight and Leafpool FINALLY made up. I am so so glad that the drama with them is finally over.<br /><br />* Hollyleaf's death scene: sure it was sad but in my humble opinion it was really well written and probably the best authored scene in the entire book.<br /><br />* Bramblstar became leader of Thunderclan. Even though I was a bit upset that the Erins went against what they had previously revealed as a spoiler (that Brambleclaw would not become leader), I believe that Brambleclaw deserved the position, and was glad to see him receive it.<br /><br /><b>Dislikes:</b><br /><br />* The scenes with Rock and Flametail I just thought were absolutely pointless and added nothing to overall development of the story. Well maybe the Flametail scene helped a bit with convincing the Clans to bond together but that's about it. The Rock scene I absolutely loathed. He didn't say anything that Jayfeather, Lionblaze and Dovewing did not already know except the 'if y'all weren't born there would be no Dark Forest!' (I paraphrased there) I think that was supposed to make the story more dramatic and suspenseful, but to me all it did was make the story... cheesy.<br /><br />* The simple fact that the Clans were easily convinced to bond together by the Three (and Starclan sorta) against the Dark Forest just <i>zap</i> like that. There was no serious arguing, no clan that took a lot longer to decide, no leader that decided to go rogue and join his Clan with the Dark Forest, nothing. I just do not see how at the end of book 5 the Clans can be at each others throats and will not even look at each other, but by book 6 they are all hunky dory and easily persuaded without any real fuss to team up against the DF (Dark Forest). Really? Don't tell me all trouble in <i>The Forgotten Warrior</i> was caused by the Flametail incident and when Jayfeather wrapped it up everyone was all cotton candy and sparkles with each other? I really think the whole book (and especially the final battle scene) would have been a whole lot more exciting if there had been more trouble with the Clans getting along (like maybe where the DF is picking off each Clan one at a time and finally the Clans that are left decide to align themselves together and fight off the DF).<br /><br />* The Erins did not utilize their new villains as much as I thought they should. IMHO the book would have been a lot better if Sol had played a big role (since he played such a big one in the previous book) and if Breezepelt and even Mappleshade had made a bigger impact in the overall storyline. I just sort of felt like the Erins used the DF fight solely for the purpose of having Tigerstar make a cameo appearance and do his get back at Firestar thing. Actually this was the biggest reason I was largely skeptical about the whole 'DF vs Starclan' thing. It seemed like nothing more than a recycling of old antagonists and old plots. <br /><br />* The book just seemed extremely rushed, especially the final battle. I could not understand how the previous five books were really slow dramatic build up and then have the final fight scene be nothing more than a really rushed battle where the cats just sort of claw at each other, and the Clans win without even really trying. This was supposed to be 10 times better than the Bloodclan battle. The Bloodclan battle was 10 times better than this.<br /><br />* IT WAS JUST WAY TOO COMPLETELY CLICHE! Everything from the cheesy Tigerstar vs Firestar face off (I thought the Erins had Tigerstar killed by Scourge so that they could avoid a scene such as this?), to Firestar's subsequent death, was just nothing but overused plots. The 'big plot twist' (as if) is that it turns out that Firestar is the fourth cat and that the 'Fire only will save our Clan' was really about the DF battle, and not about the dogs, Bloodclan or Tigerstar in the original series. Of course I never completely understood what Firestar was supposed to do as the 'fourth cat' (actually the way things turned out, the three's powers were not really needed all that much). The 'follow your heart' thing with Cinderheart, was just... IDK, bad. And now I really do not understand why Cinderpelt reincarnated as Cinderheart, if she would only return to StarClan as herself later, without getting to live her whole life out as a warrior (wasn't that the whole reason for Cinderpelt coming back in the first place?) Finally, Spottedleaf's death scene was probably the most cliche thing in the whole book. <br /><br />All in all I think I believe I am done with Warriors and Erin Hunter in general. I do not see myself reading the new super edition: Yellowfang's Secret, or the new prequel Warriors arc called Dawn of the Clans. I might try the new <i>Survivors</i> series but only because that series is written by different authors than Warriors ( authors using the Erin pen name like Warriors authors used the Erin pen name) so I do not believe I should judge that series by the fact that Warriors has just become too cliche. I believe that Warriors is like a dead horse that has long been beaten to a pulp. It is time to leave the series, and allow it to rest in peace. Only sometimes I wonder if Harper Collins (and possibly the Erins) are only stretching the series out because of the money involved. They seem to view Warriors as a franchise not a book series.<br /><br />Edit: Okay, so I have spent some time thinking, and I have changed my mind. I think I will try Dawn of the Clans because I am willing to give the Erins a second chance. And also since Dawn of the Clans is a prequel series about the when the Warrior Clans first came to be, there is practically a 0% chance that the series will fall victim to putting old main characters that have long been in the background back into the limelight, and of a reusing of old villains when there are plenty of new, fresh antagonists that can be utilized (which was my largest problem with POT and OOTS). So I'll try it, with extreme skepticism that the series will be any good, but also a glimmer of hope that it will be something of a masterpiece.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13265510975251384421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2767663673318314114" style="display:none">WOW. OMG. SO INTENSE; SO EPIC; SO INCREDIBLE; SO PERFECT! I LOVED THIS BOOK SO, SO MUCH AND IT HAS TO BE ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ! JUST WOW...<br /><br />Firstly, this is the final book in the OOTS series and the final book where we're with the current cats. We've grown with them since Into the Wild many, many books ago and now it's over. We won't be journeying with the current cats any more and it's so sad. We must take a moment... <br /><br />There is going to be a 5th Warriors series after this, but set at the dawn of the clans. And whilst that's going to be very, very epic, it's sad to know that we won't be continuing with the current cats which I've really grown to love. I wish we could as I love them all in different ways. Thank you to all the Erin's - Vicky, Kate, Cherith and Tui - for writing such a fabulous, well loved series. We can't wait for the fifth series, but this is a sad moment anyway...<br /><br />WARNING: PREPARE FOR ULTIMATE GUSH :D<br /><br />Characters - 5/5 - PERFECT! I loved each and every single one of them in different, unique ways. I mean, I felt so much sympathy towards them throughout and when they were all battling at the end my mouth was open in shock at most parts when things happened towards the characters. I was basically speechless! And I’ve found that throughout this series the characters have all grown on me and this book really made me realise how much they had. I cared about cats that I didn’t even bother about before – it was so surprising to see how sad I was regarding some of their deaths. As mentioned earlier, it’s going to be very sad to not be continuing with this current group of cats as we’ve grown up with them throughout the series. I can’t express how much I love all the characters to be totally honest. There’s so many different personalities in there that it’s great for everyone!<br /><br />Plot – 4.5/5 – Urgh, I was SO TEMPTED to give this a 5 and was so close to giving one! Seriously, I was! But I’m always honest no matter what series it is and have to say that maybe it could have fired into the battle a little sooner? Though it could just be because I was highly anticipating the battle, as has every reader of the series for many books! I was like: “PLEASE! HURRY UP; I WANT THE BATTLE RIGHT NOW!” But nevertheless, there was so much intrigue and emotion before then and I think building up to the battle was certainly suspenseful! But let’s talk about the battle! OH MY GOSH WAS THAT A BATTLE!! I mean, seriously one of the best Warriors battles ever – a great way to end of the book and the series! I was so shocked with my mouth wide open throughout and I couldn’t put the book down at all. It was so intense and gripping – you just had to find out what happened! I’m sorry for going on and on but seriously, you must read Warriors if you haven’t already. You don’t know what you’re missing out on and all fans will most certainly agree! <br /><br />Writing – 5/5 – What else could I give other than a five? Seriously, you guys know how much I love the Erin’s writing style. It’s full of beautiful description with vivid, awesome adjectives, yet at the same time it’s not overdone and it’s a simple, easy-to-read style. I really did whizz through this book because of that! And it’s such a fast-paced style as well that it works perfectly with things such as the battle, but nothing feels rushed. The suspense was built up very nicely! And then there was great emotional build-up through the writing and as a reader you’re simply drawn in. You can’t do anything else but read! And the pleasure of a style like this is that it can be enjoyed by anyone both young and old – Warriors is definitely for all ages! So yes, PERFECT writing style and I couldn’t ask for better!!<br /><br />Enjoyment – 5/5 – If you didn’t guess I was giving it a 5 you must have been dreaming off in a bin for the most part of this video! You can tell how much I loved it! IT’S PHENOMENAL! Superb characters, plot and writing style – one of the best Warriors books I’ve ever read and also one of the best books I’ve ever read out of all books. I really can’t talk about how much I love it and give it justice without all this gush. I just can’t recommend the book and the whole Warriors series enough!! Go read it right now!!<br /><br />Overall – 4.9/5 – I really wish it was a perfect rating, but you know, it ALMOST is!! I have to re-read this again soon because I just found it to be fabulous. I really can’t thank everyone working on the Warriors books enough because since the first book they’ve been my favourite series ever and they’ll continue that way until they end whenever that may be. And my mind is still in shock about that battle and will be for ages! I couldn’t quite believe everything and was on the edge of my seat - a definite page turner.<br /><br />Hope this wasn’t TOO gushy. I guess it is, but how else can I explain how much I love it? (Actually I typed a review before which deleted itself which was MORE gushy, but you know…) </span>

<div id="review_308117785" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308117785" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3115456-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393929912p2/3115456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308117785?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3115456-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308117785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2151656102297036403">The Warriors series was something that changed my life. I stumbled upon the first book in my uncle's home almost three years ago (the summer before Year 7), and was hooked ever since. So when the epic finale came out, I had to read it. Unfortunately, being in China, I couldn't get a copy until this morning.<br/><br/>With such an epic franchise to conclude, I was a bit worried that this book would be a disappointment. But while it was not a complete raging page-turner (which isn't that possible), it was fa</span>
  <span id="freeText2151656102297036403" style="display:none">The Warriors series was something that changed my life. I stumbled upon the first book in my uncle's home almost three years ago (the summer before Year 7), and was hooked ever since. So when the epic finale came out, I had to read it. Unfortunately, being in China, I couldn't get a copy until this morning.<br /><br />With such an epic franchise to conclude, I was a bit worried that this book would be a disappointment. But while it was not a complete raging page-turner (which isn't that possible), it was far from bad. Absolutely stellar, in fact. Characterization is strong and fully developed for most of the characters who get screen (or page) time, which is impressive considering the large number of them. While others complained of poor characterization and Mary Sues, I never found flaws in this.<br /><br />Plot points are all tied up in this, in which the motives behind the antagonists' actions are explained convincingly, and so are those of the protagonists (or the rare "caught in the middle" character). To finish more than twenty books' worth of intricacies and stories in one is commendable, and rather successful.<br /><br />All in all, an excellent read. Does arguably just as well as HP's Deathly Hallows in terms of concluding, and just maybe even better. The ending is just awesome. Wrapping up everything perfectly, but still leaving enough to the readers' imagination (i.e the relationship aspects, which some fans consider extremely important).<br /><br />Read it. You'll love it if you can let go of the "children's book" stigma. This is not just for kids. Adults will enjoy the subtle political undertones, and teenagers that have read the series appreciate the action and the "growing-up" phase the characters go through.<br /><br />PS: The series "matures" with its readers, and progressively turns darker. Something I consider respectable, as Harry Potter does this quite well. Unlike other artistic ventures (mostly in music), which have let their fans down for commercial success, Warriors continues to deliver the goods.\\<br /><br />Read on!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2151656102297036403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_312982656" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312982656" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5502367-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306291518p2/5502367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312982656?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/5502367-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13114292-the-last-hope">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Redwall, Wind in the Willows, Watership Down; catlovers who don't mind formula YA fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502367-lori?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502367-lori?shelf=tween-young-adult">tween-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502367-lori?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502367-lori?shelf=cats">cats</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312982656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11866197050793590231">*****SPOILER*****<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>I try to rate the Warriors series as what it is - not "great literature", but formula storytelling for juvenile or tween readers, holding more in common with Nancy Drew than Huck Finn. None of the installations have earned 5 stars from me, but several have earned 4, despite flaws such as repetitiveness, painfully manipulative cliffhanger moments and major-character introspection, anthropomorphizing to the point of nonsense, and glaring biological impossibilities. It is fantasy, </span>
  <span id="freeText11866197050793590231" style="display:none">*****SPOILER*****<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I try to rate the Warriors series as what it is - not "great literature", but formula storytelling for juvenile or tween readers, holding more in common with Nancy Drew than Huck Finn. None of the installations have earned 5 stars from me, but several have earned 4, despite flaws such as repetitiveness, painfully manipulative cliffhanger moments and major-character introspection, anthropomorphizing to the point of nonsense, and glaring biological impossibilities. It is fantasy, after all, and as such it's allowed an improbable species of semi-socialist feral pussycats existing in a mystical alternate Earthworld, as long as the narrative maintains integrity and consistency within its kittyverse - which, for the most part, the series as a whole does.<br /><br />That said, this book disappointed me. It ties up loose storylines too neatly, resolves all long-festering interClan conflicts simplistically, and is overly sentimental with major heroic characters while dispatching undead archvillains and longtime secondary characters with perfunctory indifference. There is little emotional subtlety or introspection here. The plot is functional and action-driven - serving equally as a finale to Firestar's saga, and as a bridge to a possible subsequent series - but the mechanical formula is appallingly obvious in the writing. I'm not sure whether I want to see a "next generation" series, as the writers' effort and creativity peaked a couple of story arcs ago and seems in decline. Maybe they just need the inspiration of a fresh batch of major characters. (I would like to see Ivypool develop as a likely mantle-inheritor - she kicks serious ass while also displaying antihero potential.) Or maybe the franchise has played out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11866197050793590231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9989854543645879117">Oh my gosh. I <i> HATED </i> the end to the series. The first series was amazing, and it went downhill from there. This book was the worst of them all. I could rant for hours on how bad this book was. First off, in the final battle, the three had nothing big to do in it. The clan cats would have been fine without them. And how many cats died? Like, only six. -.- Seriously? It's a battle against the greatest villians of all time, who have killed hundreds, and only SIX cats die? What is up with that. The</span>
  <span id="freeText9989854543645879117" style="display:none">Oh my gosh. I <i> HATED </i> the end to the series. The first series was amazing, and it went downhill from there. This book was the worst of them all. I could rant for hours on how bad this book was. First off, in the final battle, the three had nothing big to do in it. The clan cats would have been fine without them. And how many cats died? Like, only six. -.- Seriously? It's a battle against the greatest villians of all time, who have killed hundreds, and only SIX cats die? What is up with that. They all should have been Massacred. Really.<br /><br />Next thing. It was predictable. Except the part of Firestar being the ''fourth'' cat. I mean, come on. He sits around on his furry bee-hind, being nothing but a lazy old fart, and suddenly he swoops back in and becomes a hero of the last book. Really? You expect people to actually like him? I only liked him in the first series, the rest I hated him. Every time he lost a life, I'd be like, "PLEASE let him freaking die already."<br /><br />The sad thing is, I had freaked out over this book. I thought that maybe they could redeem themselves by actually writing a good book. I thought that the Erins might end on a good note. I counted down the days until the book, hoping, thinking it would be amazing. I thought wrong. My hopes were off, very off. It was one of the worst pieces of trash I have ever read. My favorite part was when Firestar died. Couldn't Bramblestar have died too? <br /><br />Sorry to rat on the book that plenty on people might have liked, but I hated it. I wouldn't recommend it to anyone who wanted to read a good book. Just skip it and look what happens up on Wikipedia. Save your precious time. Please.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307860739" />
    <a title="Natalia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7027546-natalia"><img alt="Natalia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408583409p2/7027546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307860739?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalia" href="/user/show/7027546-natalia">Natalia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061555275" href="/book/show/12036852-the-last-hope">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307860739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5974661644432815217">Man, this series was my childhood in a nutshell. My obsession with this series would border ridiculous at some points in time. My happiness was overwhelming when I saw a novel of this series at Barnes&Noble, it being the first novel in English I actually read. Those were the days . . .<br/><br/>Now, this is the last novel in the fourth series The Omen of the Stars. It is the grande finale, where the Dark Forest rises to its full power and the true battle begins. Where warriors' loyalties are constantly te</span>
  <span id="freeText5974661644432815217" style="display:none">Man, this series was my childhood in a nutshell. My obsession with this series would border ridiculous at some points in time. My happiness was overwhelming when I saw a novel of this series at Barnes&amp;Noble, it being the first novel in English I actually read. Those were the days . . .<br /><br />Now, this is the last novel in the fourth series The Omen of the Stars. It is the grande finale, where the Dark Forest rises to its full power and the true battle begins. Where warriors' loyalties are constantly tested and sides must be chosen. Clanmates might have to fight among each other in the final battle to survive.<br /><br />I truly enjoyed this conclusion to the series. It was powerful and left a lasting impression on me. Most of the time I truly despise how series end, and how authors do not seem to know how to wrap up their final novel. The Erins, on the other hand, are above that. They make use of this opportunity to create a truly memorable ending.<br /><br />The Final Battle between the Clans and the Dark Forest is as exciting as I believe it is meant to be. You feel the characters' fear, pain, shock, even the adrenaline as they fight for their lives. Just like Harry Potter, the Warriors series became darker and darker as it went along, and it ended up adding charm to the final novel.<br /><br />I believe the Erins did a splendid job with this one. I was truly wary of picking it up, because conclusions to series, as I mentioned, are usually disappointing. Here, the authors built up a truly powerful conclusion that keeps the reader guessing whether it will continue or not.<br /><blockquote> [ <a href="http://book-hermit.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Hermit</a> ] </blockquote> </span>

    <a title="Momo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8310553-momo"><img alt="Momo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332350686p2/8310553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325074684?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Momo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Momo" href="/user/show/8310553-momo">Momo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325074684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11477051309001738479">How many reviewers so far have claimed that this series changed their life? Is it cliche and overused for me to say it?<br/>I swear that these books changed my life.<br/>I hated reading, and then I picked up a Warriors book.<br/>After a while of reading these I began to think, "When are these going to end?!" but I regret those thoughts. The end of this book series is a true tragedy.<br/><br/>Okay, enough of the sentimentality (for now), here's my review:<br/>SPOILERS FROM THIS POINT. ENTER AT OWN RISK!<br/>Knowing that this was t</span>
  <span id="freeText11477051309001738479" style="display:none">How many reviewers so far have claimed that this series changed their life? Is it cliche and overused for me to say it?<br />I swear that these books changed my life.<br />I hated reading, and then I picked up a Warriors book.<br />After a while of reading these I began to think, "When are these going to end?!" but I regret those thoughts. The end of this book series is a true tragedy.<br /><br />Okay, enough of the sentimentality (for now), here's my review:<br />SPOILERS FROM THIS POINT. ENTER AT OWN RISK!<br />Knowing that this was the end of the series, I read through the book quite cautiously, hoping with every word I read that Firestar wouldn't die. I thought that if any cat died, so be it. Just not Firestar.<br />I'm not afraid to admit that I cried when he died, and then I grew completely numb. I thought of the beginning, how it all started with little Rusty's first venture into the forest...I'm starting to tear up again now, just thinking about it.<br />However, his death was completely random. I thought for sure he and Tigerstar would die battling each other. When he didn't die, I was hopeful...I had to read through his short, meaningless death twice to make sure I wasn't missing something. What kind of death was that for the cat who meant the most to the clans ever?! It was a complete disappointment.<br /><br />Another disappointment was with Dovewing. Yes, I have a shipping obsession: Dovewing and Tigerheart. Since Bumblestripe was hinted at being Dovewing's love interest, I'd been watching him carefully. At the end of this book, when Dovewing clearly chose him over Tigerheart, I was more angry than I had been since Cinderpelt died.<br /><br />Although there were some obvious disappointments in my opinion, I loved every moment of reading this. My childhood is over...I guess that means I should grow up now.</span>

  <span id="freeText9467624907419440597" style="display:none">(It's been a while since I finished this, but I've finally got around to writing this review. I actually wrote this review the minute after I finished it, but that was my hand written one, not the one on here.)<br /><br />I can't do it. I can't write a review of this. I'm lying on my bed, nose and eyes still burning from crying so much, and I just...can't. <br /><br />This series...is the reason I love reading. I still remember the day Mama put <i>Warriors: Into the Wild</i> in my hands when I was ten years old. And I didn't want to read it! Can you believe it? I didn't like reading back then, but once I started <i>Into the Wild</i>, I couldn't stop. <br />Soon, I made Mama get me the boxed set of the first Warriors series and devoured that. And ever since, I've bought every new Warriors book to come out and even reread the entire series just last year. <br />And now? With the last book done, four years and twenty-four books later, it's just an incredible and immensely sad feeling. <br />If I hadn't read this series, I probably wouldn't have gotten into reading, and I would still be that TV addicted little kid with a boring and uneventful life. Now, my whole <i>life</i> depends on reading, and I owe it all to the women that make up Erin Hunter. <br />Thank you, Erin Hunter, for creating something I will cherish until I die. <br />Look at me, I'm already a nostalgic old woman. <br /><br />Truly brilliant series. I will be reading it time and time again. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_321063891" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321063891" />
    <a title="♏⟑¢⊀∑∏≳≀∑" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6391355"><img alt="♏⟑¢⊀∑∏≳≀∑" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317830638p2/6391355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321063891?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♏⟑¢⊀∑∏≳≀∑" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♏⟑¢⊀∑∏≳≀∑" href="/user/show/6391355">♏⟑¢⊀∑∏≳≀∑</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6391355?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer321063891&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321063891" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7072770458269002770">With battles one and lost, challenges conquered and forgotten, the all Clans have faced all of their battles with courage and unwavering loyalty. Each clan has suffered deaths and yet rejoiced in the comings of new kits. “There will be three cats, kin of your kin, with the power of the stars in their paws. They will find a fourth, and the battle between light and dark will be won. A new leader will rise from the shadows of his death, and the Clans will survive beyond the memories of his memories</span>
  <span id="freeText7072770458269002770" style="display:none">With battles one and lost, challenges conquered and forgotten, the all Clans have faced all of their battles with courage and unwavering loyalty. Each clan has suffered deaths and yet rejoiced in the comings of new kits. “There will be three cats, kin of your kin, with the power of the stars in their paws. They will find a fourth, and the battle between light and dark will be won. A new leader will rise from the shadows of his death, and the Clans will survive beyond the memories of his memories. This is how it has been, and how it will always be.” (Hunter p. 329) This quote proves that even though times of hardship, the Clans will still survive and good will come of it.<br /><br />My opinion on the theme is that it was great because it was fiction, about cats, and, best of all, the series finale. The delivery of the story was great because it didn’t deliver the information too quick so that you got overwhelmed, yet quick enough so that you didn't get bored with it. I would say that the age group for reading this is about 9-12 years old because the phrasing of the sentences is simple and a bit young. I would definitely recommend this book for anyone who is interested in fantasy, cats, and people who are willing to make a commitment to a long series. There are about 45 books total (including manga and super editions)<br /><br />I would give this book a 4 out of 5 because it has action, adventure, and cats. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The only reason it is not a 5, is because Firestar dies.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I like how there are different roles for different cats, like medicine cat, warrior, leader, deputy ect. I got a bit confused at the very end, where Firestar dies and Brambleclaw becomes Bramblestar. Shouldn’t Bramblestar have gone to the MoonPool to receive his nine lives and <i>then</i> be called Bramblestar? Yet, overall, it was very well written.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7072770458269002770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15554235310734720804" style="display:none">*This review was originally published on <a href="https://rachelpoli.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">RachelPoli.com</a><br /><br />BOOK COVER<br /><br />As soon as I picked up this book, I knew exactly who the cat on the front cover was. And I cried. I had spoiled something for myself a while ago and, with the content of the Omen of the Stars books, I knew something was coming. The title alone says it all.<br /><br />PLOT<br /><br />This is the final book in the Omen of the Stars series. This particular series of Warriors has been my favorite so far because it had so many Harry Potter vibes. I’ve been with these characters since I was 11-years-old and this plot wrapped everything up so nicely and punched me right in the gut.<br /><br />This would have been the perfect ending to the series as a whole. Of course, there are three series (at the time of writing this review) after this one. So, this book serves as an ending and new beginning.<br /><br />WRITING STYLE<br /><br />This book, as I said earlier, punched me right in the gut. I don’t even know how to write this review because of spoilers… though, based on my blog audience, I’m not sure how many of you will actually go read these books. Still, I took out the character section due to spoilers because I don’t know what to say.<br /><br />I cried throughout the majority of this book – that’s how good the writing is. I’m still crying even while writing this review.<br /><br />OVERALL<br /><br />This was a wonderful ending to a new beginning. I’m glad the series is still going, but I would have been satisfied if this was the final book in the Warriors series. I’m looking forward to reading a brand new generation of Warriors.<br /><br />Favorite Quote:<br /><br />“I would have taken your place if you had let me.” -Erin Hunter, Warriors: The Last Hope (Omen of the Stars 6)</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer707888137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16605950024717867836">I was highly disappointed in this book... In fact, I hardly enjoyed any of the books in the "Omen of the Stars". Ever since the first series (which I absolutely adored), it just kinda start rolling down hill and The Last Hope was at the bottom. The plot just didn't add up in the end, and when Firestar was suddenly thrown back into it, I was like "<i>What!?</i>" After he became a side character after the first series, it makes absolutely <i>no</i> sense to suddenly put him back in the spotlight. But if it were</span>
  <span id="freeText16605950024717867836" style="display:none">I was highly disappointed in this book... In fact, I hardly enjoyed any of the books in the "Omen of the Stars". Ever since the first series (which I absolutely adored), it just kinda start rolling down hill and The Last Hope was at the bottom. The plot just didn't add up in the end, and when Firestar was suddenly thrown back into it, I was like "<i>What!?</i>" After he became a side character after the first series, it makes absolutely <i>no</i> sense to suddenly put him back in the spotlight. But if it were up to me, Firestar would have been killed off a loooong time ago.<br /><br />It lacked in the amazing detail that "The Darkest Hour" had, and the style it was written in was difficult to read. In fact, I had to <i>re-read</i> the last couple of chapters because I honestly had no idea what was going on. You would suspect this huge, bloody battle, with tons of detail, but all that happened was Dovewing jumping around, clawing come cats, and suddenly Firestar was the fourth cat in this prophecy which really didn't make a lot of sense. <br /><br />And why would Brambleclaw make Squirrelflight his deputy after he became leader? Just so he could show her that he "forgave her"? Thinking back on all of Squirrelflight's mistakes, she should have been the last cat to choose. Anyways, not a book I would recommend, unless I hated the person. I'm thinking that a better ending would have been to just kill off ALL the characters, and be done with it. Or maybe, even stopped writing after the 2nd or 3rd series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16605950024717867836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1514179824578924873">The Great Battle draws near and the three needs to become 4 to battle the darkness that lasts forever... Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovewing are confused. How could The Three need another? Lionblaze thinks it's their long lost sister Hollyleaf. Dovewing is convinced that it's her sister, Ivypool. Jayfeather believes that it has to be a dead ancestor named Tigerheart after he saw a reed with a smoldering tip. Meanwhile, in the dark forest, Tigerstar has gathered up warriors from all of the clans </span>
  <span id="freeText1514179824578924873" style="display:none">The Great Battle draws near and the three needs to become 4 to battle the darkness that lasts forever... Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovewing are confused. How could The Three need another? Lionblaze thinks it's their long lost sister Hollyleaf. Dovewing is convinced that it's her sister, Ivypool. Jayfeather believes that it has to be a dead ancestor named Tigerheart after he saw a reed with a smoldering tip. Meanwhile, in the dark forest, Tigerstar has gathered up warriors from all of the clans to turn on their clanmates when the day they will rise. Alive and dead warriors are planning to take over the clans and send them pummeling into StarClan, where dead cats can enjoy their afterlives. That is, if StarClan still survives after the darkness. When Ivypool is recruited she says yes and later turns into a spy for ThunderClan, the place she actually belongs. She passes on information of the dark forest onto their leader, Firestar, who starts to plan what they need to do. The book is one of my all-time favorites, and I think people who enjoy cats will enjoy this book. It's a series book and you should start at Book 1: Into the wild. But be warned: When you finish the series, you'll never look at your plain old tabby cat the same again!</span>

<div id="review_87594170" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712048-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567374751p2/712048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87594170?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/712048-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061555275" href="/book/show/12036852-the-last-hope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712048-kayla?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87594170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4856755790210497349">Well here it goes. The final (not really) installment of the Warriors series. I remember when my sister started reading this series. I thought it would be to childish and for a few months I scorned the series. But after she was hooked on them I decided I would give the series a try. And boy what a ride. I would have never thought cats could be given such human characteristics (and believe me I'm an animal lover/activist). Quickly I fell in love with the clan cats. I knew the final battle was dra</span>
  <span id="freeText4856755790210497349" style="display:none">Well here it goes. The final (not really) installment of the Warriors series. I remember when my sister started reading this series. I thought it would be to childish and for a few months I scorned the series. But after she was hooked on them I decided I would give the series a try. And boy what a ride. I would have never thought cats could be given such human characteristics (and believe me I'm an animal lover/activist). Quickly I fell in love with the clan cats. I knew the final battle was drawing near and I assumed what would happen in the end, but it was still quite sad to read.<br /><br />I though the beginning was a bit slow, as I was slightly annoyed that Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovewing spent so much time trying to find the fourth cat. Then it turns out he's right under their noses. And in the final battle I was imagining something like all the clans uniting on the island and fighting side by side. But oh well. I was still glued to this book from cover to cover.<br /><br />For all those who stuck through the series and know how amazing it is. I know you to will feel the sadness of a much loved warriors death as much as I do right now. :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="4856755790210497349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10791681857012739750">Wow. Just.... Wow. This book was soo good. People at my school make fun of my love for this series because it's about cats, but honestly it is about so much more than that. It's about friendship and learning to accept people for who they are. <br/><br/>I know so many people have said this series has changed their lives, and honestly it did for me too. It was the first book series that really made me love reading, and that I really fell for the characters and I fell HARD. This book ends the series perfectl</span>
  <span id="freeText10791681857012739750" style="display:none">Wow. Just.... Wow. This book was soo good. People at my school make fun of my love for this series because it's about cats, but honestly it is about so much more than that. It's about friendship and learning to accept people for who they are. <br /><br />I know so many people have said this series has changed their lives, and honestly it did for me too. It was the first book series that really made me love reading, and that I really fell for the characters and I fell HARD. This book ends the series perfectly, and it really pulls it all together. It was kind of like saying goodbye to my childhood. Is that cliche? Sure. Is it true? Heck yes. <br /><br />It kills me to say I'm probably done with Warriors, but I know I never really will be, the characters and their lessons are always lingering in the back of my mind and it makes me happy to say I didn't judge the book by it's cover, and I absolutely LOVED IT. Thanks ERIN HUNTER!!</span>

<div id="review_2935868901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2935868901" />
    <a title="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat"><img alt="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491529769p2/6759885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2935868901?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)" href="/user/show/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat">Jessi (Novel Heartbeat)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/32328624-the-last-hope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6759885-jessi-novel-heartbeat?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2935868901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7109863718998591848"><b>4.5/5</b><br/><br/>Welp that was traumatizing.<br/><br/>Remember how I've been complaining that the old series I loved had vanished - for like the past 12 books? Well, apparently they decided to cram 12 books of emotion into this one last book.<br/><br/>I'm equal parts relieved, devastated, and pissed. Relieved that I finally got to see a glimmer of what I loved so much about the series before I called it quits. Devastated because my favorite character and other beloved characters are now dead. PISSED because they waited so long</span>
  <span id="freeText7109863718998591848" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br />Welp that was traumatizing.<br /><br />Remember how I've been complaining that the old series I loved had vanished - for like the past 12 books? Well, apparently they decided to cram 12 books of emotion into this one last book.<br /><br />I'm equal parts relieved, devastated, and pissed. Relieved that I finally got to see a glimmer of what I loved so much about the series before I called it quits. Devastated because my favorite character and other beloved characters are now dead. PISSED because they waited so long to actually DO something with my emotions that it now feels like a plot device.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew Firestar was going to die. I knew that two series ago and felt it in my bones going into this series. I knew he'd die in the final battle. But I am HELLA PISSED that he went out the way he did. I love that he saved his clan, but a fucking lightning strike and flaming tree?? Really? It's absolutely fucking stupid that he survived the major battle (we finally got to see that epic showdown with Tigerstar that I was hoping for the first time he died!!) with little to no wounds only to be taken down by a falling, burning tree that got hit by lightning. He should have died from his wounds after taking Tigerstar out. *rolls eyes*<br /><br />I wasn't at all surprised at the return of Hollyleaf. I had started to suspect she wasn't dead (and also there was no closure in her death because she just disappeared - I never believe a character is actually dead in fiction unless we SEE it happen - and sometimes not even then, fucking fiction). I cried when she died, but I was also kinda pissed about that one too. It feels like she came back JUST to die for real. At least she went out with honor this time! I sobbed when Mousefur died, but it wasn't as hard as I expected with her being my favorite character. I was thrilled that she got to go out fighting and got the warrior's death that she deserved! Spottedleaf's death hit me harder than I expected. We've already seen her die once, and she seemed untouchable in StarClan, so it felt so unfair for her to die again. I lost my fucking shit when Firestar protested that she promised to be there to welcome him into StarClan and she told him it wasn't meant to be. I was also really surprised by how hard Ferncloud's death hit me. I didn't realize how attached I was to her, and when Dustpelt found his dead mate I lost my shit again :( Poor Dustpelt! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved that there was a little bit of catharsis between Leafpool and Crowfeather, as well as Leafpool and her kits. And Brambleclaw and Squirrelflight as well! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He made her his deputy, dawwwww *sobs* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The little moment between Longtail and Mousefur got me all misty too:<br /><i>"You took your time," Mousefur muttered. "Always late, that's your trouble."<br />"Not too late, I hope," Longtail retorted.</i><br />Oh Mousefur how I love you, you bitter and snarky little cinnamon roll. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But then she died right after that. BRB SOBBING. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I wasn't really a fan of the whole Tigerheart/Dovewing ship. I wanted her to get with Bumblestripe so bad! I didn't care for the love triangle they had going. Dovewing was kind of an idiot in that regard. <br /><br />All in all, this one finally brought the old series back and I'm glad I got to have my emotional attachment before calling quits on the series. I am kind of aggravated that it was all crammed into the span of 25 pages, though -__-</span>
  <a data-text-id="7109863718998591848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8785964433652017949" style="display:none">There are numorus characters and I can't just pick and choose who is my favorite so I will do all of them...(Most of them).......<br /><br />Firestar: Firestar is brave- this is because he fought Tigerstar when he was on his last life...<br /><br />Dovewing: Dovewing in my opinion is so stupid and naive she is likable. Her character stregnth is Kindness<br /><br />Ivypool: She is also brave just like Firestar. She also has social intellect. She also has self-control. Ivypool is definetly my favorite character because she is very smart and controled. This is shown by her spying in the dark forest and not giving anything away, not cracking, and making sacrifices.<br /><br />Lionblaze: Lionblaze's character stregnth is Love and zest. Wich is Ironic because his special ability is to never be beaten in a fight.<br /><br />Jayfeather: Jayfeather is a critical thinker. But he lacks Humility.<br /><br />Tigerheart: I really don't like Tigerheart. He made it such a big deal when Dovewing rejcted him over Bumblestripe. But never the less his character streghnth is Hope because he kept hope that Dovewing would like him over Bumblestripe.<br /><br />Hollyleaf: Hollyleaf would be my favorite character if she did not have so much self dought. She is though Brave and persistent and she has good perspective and she eventually learns forgiveness. I know this because she finally forgives her mother Leafpool for lieing and breaking the Warrior Code.<br /><br />Leafpool: Leafpool is very calm and loving. She keptloving her kits (Jayfeather, Lionblaze and HollyLeaf) even if they did not know that she was their mother and when they hated her for lieing to them.<br />Squirrelflight: Squirrelflight took care of Leafpool's kits and possed as their mother until Ashfur went crazy and tryed to kill er kits when she said the trueth. her stregnth is prudence, leadership and bravery.<br /><br />Ashfur: Ashfur is not in this book but he has an interesting life so... He loved Squirrelflight but she did not reciprocate his feelingss back. So he went crazy and threatened to kill squirrelflight's kits when she tolded him that they weren't her kits and that it did not matter to her. He then asked who's kits they were and Squirrelflight tolded him that they were Leafpool's and Crowfeather (who was from an other clan) so that he wouldn't harm them. He let them go and said that at the nexed gathering of the clans the would tell. Hollyleaf realized that this could not happen so she killed Ashfur to protect Her mother and her adoptive mother. He is not in the books much until this and he as a character is not that interesting. But as I can tell his character stregnth is Love. Many say that what he felt for Squirrelflight was genuine love but what I think is that it got to and obsessive state.</span>
